9
Solutions206
Given the growing concerns regarding UV filters present in the environment, the public
and agencies have been searching for solutions. Legislation has been proposed to ban chemicals
On May 1, 2018, the Hawaiian state legislature passed a
bill that bans the sale and distribution of sunscreens containing oxybenzone and octinoxate. At
the time of this writing, the bill is awaiting the signature of Governor David Y. Ige.'^^ If the bill is
signed or proceeds without a veto, the law will go into effect in 2021. Additional states have
considered similar legislation.
Several aquatic parks have published literature to educate the public regarding the risk of
organic filters for the marine environment. Xelha in Mexico advises tourists to travel with
chemical-free sunscreen” when visiting their park*’*’; and, the US National Park Service
published an educational pamphlet stating “Remember if it’s on your skin, it’s on the reef. Be
reef friendly! Reduce the amount of sunscreen you leave behind...
joined the cause by showing, during the flight, a documentary about reef bleaching and
distributing reef-safe sunscreen {containing only inorganic filters).
Photoprotection should include seeking shades when outdoors, wearing photoprotective
clothing including swim-wear, wide brimmed hats and sunglasses; only on exposed areas should
sunscreens be applied. Practicing photoprotection with the above guidelines, and applying
sunscreens with inorganic filters (titanium dioxide, zinc oxide) are an alternative means of
protecting oneself from UV radiation.
Aside from limiting continued leaching of UV filters into the environment, means of
optimizing their removal from the water supply have been explored. Studies have been done with
Cyperus alternifolius L, a common wetland plant that absorbs oxybenzone into its root system
and accumulates the chemical in its tissues. The plant ultimately converts oxybenzone to
chemical conjugates with lower toxicity. This mechanism was evaluated as a means of possibly
removing oxybenzone from the environment, with the caveat that these plants would need to be
extracted before they undergo natural decay.

that have impacted our food supply.

10
Conclusion235
With the known effects of UV radiation on erythema, photoaging, and skin cancer
development, photoprotection is paramount. However, we must also take into account the impact
of our efforts on the environment. UV filters have been identified in many water sources; they
arc extremely difficult to remove using traditional WWTP practices. With continued use of
organic filters, one can surmise that concentrations in our water sources will continue to rise. The
effect on coral reefs is clearly multifactorial; however, at increasing concentrations UV filters
may play a more instrumental role in bleaching. Furthermore, increasing ocean concentrations
will accentuate bioaccumulation and biomagnification, ultimately raising potentially negative
consequences in humans. Fortunately, the current detected levels in the environment have been
in the lower toxicity ranges for the species of coral studied in vitro, and there have been no
identifiable toxic effects on humans.
It seems clear that with this growing body of evidence of the negative impacts of organic
UV filters in our environment that we should actively explore alternative forms of
photoprotection and novel water filtration methods. The effects of inorganic filters on the
environment is still being studied but, at this time, physical blockers are recommend as
photoprotection alternatives. The concern about the environmental impact of organic UV filters
should not detract from educating the public on the importance of photoprotection, namely, to
seek shade, wear photoprotective clothing and swim-wear when outdoors, and applying
appropriate sunscreens on sun exposed areas. This would allow us to protect our skin from the
deleterious effects of sunlight, and at the same time, protect our environment.

Key Points
Several organic UV filters such as oxybenzone, octocrylene, octinoxatc and 4-
methylbenzylidenecamphor have been identified in water sources and in aquatic animals.
Oxybenzone, in laboratory settings, has been implicated as a possible contributor to coral
reef bleaching.
These concerns have prompted the Hawaii state legislature to pass a bill, in May 2018,
banning sunscreens containing oxybenzone and octinoxatc, effective in 2021.
It is important for dermatologists and health care providers to continue to encourage
photoprotectivc measures, which include seeking shade, wearing photoprotcctivc clothing
and sunglasses, and on exposed skin, applying appropriate sunscreens.

RE: Opposition to Proposed Legislation Banning Non-Mineral Sunscreens
Dear Chair Lee:
On behalf of the members of the Personal Care Products Council (PCPC),^ I am writing to express our
opposition to Bill 135, legislation to prohibit the sale, use, or distribution of non-mineral sunscreens.
This bill will lead to a serious public health issue by banning essential, safe and effective sunscreen
products that Hawaiians currently trust and rely on, particularly since the U.S. has a limited number of
approved ingredients to make these products.
The U.S. has Limited Number of Sunscreen Ingredients to Fight Skin Cancer
Sunscreens are a key factor in preventing and reducing the risk of skin cancer and damage from the
sun's ultraviolet (UV) rays. Public health organizations, including the American Cancer Society, American
Academy of Dermatology, the Mayo Clinic and the Skin Cancer Foundation, recommend using sunscreen
as part of a safe sun regimen. The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention's Sun Safety
recommendations note the importance of daily sunscreen use, including on cloudy and overcast days, to
help prevent most skin cancers. And, according to the World Health Organization (WHO), four out of five
skin cancer cases can be prevented by following safe sun practices, including using sunscreen regularly.
Sunscreen ingredients must be approved for use by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) and
are a crucial and well-recognized tool in the fight against skin cancer and premature skin aging. The U.S.
has a limited number of approved sunscreen ingredients to make products that protect consumers from
the harmful effects of solar radiation. By banning all non-mineral sunscreens, the County will be able to
provide residents and visitors with access to products containing only two of the available active
ingredients. This will significantly reduce and limit consumer choice and could result in a shortage of
available products.
’ Founded in 1894. the Personal Care Products Council (PCPC) Is the voice and advocate for 600 member companies representing the $499.6 billion global cosmetics
and personal care products industry. PCPCs members represent approximately 90% of the U.S. beauty industry and are some of the most beloved and
trusted brands in beauty and personal care today. As the manufacturers, distributers and suppliers of  adiverse range of products millions of consumers rely on
every day-from sunscreens, toothpaste and shampoo to moisturizer, makeup and fragrance-PCPCs member companies are global leaders committed to product
safety, quality and Innovation.
1620 L Street NW, Ste. 1200 | Washington, DC 20036 | (202) 331-1770 | www.personalcarecouncil.org
Page 2 of 3
Hawai'i Residents at Higher Risk for Skin Cancer
With Hawai'i's previous ban on some sunscreen active ingredients, the Maui County legislation would
further limit access to products that can help prevent skin cancer - one of the most common yet
preventable cancers. Hawai'i residents are at high risk for developing skin cancer. The American Cancer
Society estimates that melanoma, the most serious form of skin cancer, will be one of the leading causes
of new cancer cases in Hawai'i in 2021. Native Hawaiians and other Pacific Islanders sufferfrom double
the melanoma mortality rate than the State average, according to Hawai'i Health Matters, an innovative
web-based community information tool developed by the Hawai'i Health Data Warehouse and the
Hawai'i Department of Health. Hawai'i has one of the highest daily UV index averages in the nation,
making protecting residents from sun exposure a public health priority.
Legality of Proposed Ordinance in Question
Prior to adoption, PCPC and our member companies believe it is important to assess the legality of the
proposed ordinance, especially regarding jurisdictional authority, federal preemption, and commerce
clause implications. As a threshold matter, there is the question of whether the County has the authority
to regulate consumer behavior allegedly impacting offshore environmental resources. Such authority
would seem to be exclusively within the purview of Hawai'i's Department of Land and Natural
Resources/Division of Aquatic Resources, as set forth under the State's comprehensive and uniform
scheme of statutory regulation for this area of law.
Likewise, there is the question of whether the ordinances are preempted by the federal Food, Drug and
Cosmetic Act, which prohibit states and localities from establishing any provision for nonprescription
drugs that is different from or in addition to federal requirements. The purpose of such preemption is to
provide "national uniformity" with respect to product manufacturing and composition, labeling, and
advertising for nonprescription drugs. Similarly, since most sunscreens are imported into Hawai'i from
out of state, potential commerce clause ramifications with Maui County's proposed ordinances need to
be investigated. Coupled with the logistical difficulty of enforcing the bans proposed by these
ordinances, we believe these legal concerns merit  adetailed examination before this committee can
proceed with adoption.
Environmental Impact of Sunscreens is being Evaluated by the National Academies of Science,
Engineering, and Medicine (NASEM)
This ordinance does not consider the full body of scientific evidence to establish whether organic and
inorganic UV filters pose an ecological threat to Hawaiian reef systems. This includes considerations
such as the suitability and reliability of existing data to assess environmental risks in addition to the well-
recognized causes of coral reef decline in Hawai'i and the rest of the world, including climate change,
land-based pollution, and other human activities, such as physical damage to corals from recreational
activities.^
^ Mitchelmore, C. L, Bufns, E. E., Conway, A., Heyes, A., & Davies, I. A. (2021). A critical review organic ultraviolet filter exposure, hazard, and risk to corals.
Environmental Toxicology and Chemistry, 40(4), 967-988. https://doi.org/10.1002/etc.4948. See also Burns, E.E. & Davies, I.A. (2021). Coral Ecotoxicological Data
Evaluation for the Environmental Safety Assessment of Ultraviolet Filters. Environmental Toxicology and Chemistry. DOI: 10.1002/etc.5229. See also Dyer, S.O. &
Green, N.5. (2021). Use of Eco-epidemiology to Assess the Potential Risks of UV Filters to Corals. Presentation to National Academies of Science, Engineering and

Page 3 of 3
Policy decisions that will adversely impact public health should not be made ahead of a scientific
consensus on this issue. To reduce bias and to synthesize the best available science, the United States
Congress directed the NASEM to evaluate the presence and potential impacts of organic and inorganic
UV filters in freshwater and marine environments, as well as the potential public health impact of
limiting access to sunscreens. The findings of the review, which is sponsored by the U.S. Environmental
Protection Agency, are expected in early 2022. Making environmental management decisions on
sunscreens based on current insufficient and, in some cases, unreliable scientific data may lead to
unintended negative health consequences, such as fewer available sunscreens and an increase in the
prevalence of skin cancer while providing limited, if any, environmental improvement. PCPC encourages
that industry, academia, NGOs, federal agencies and the state of Hawai'i work together to ensure that
both the reef ecosystems and the health of Hawai'i's residents are protected.
By passing this local ordinance, the Maui County Council will create confusion and potentially discourage
the use of sunscreens - an important part of a daily safe-sun regimen - putting consumers' health at
greater risk. We respectfully ask that you oppose Bill 135.
Thank you for your consideration and the opportunity to comment.
Sincerely,
Karin Ross
Executive Vice President, Government Affairs

Public access to Sunscreens CrnCE Or THE(-'O! iMTV r'l cr.n'
TO: Maui County Council
Councilmember Alice Lee, Chair
Councilmember Keani Rawlins, Vice Chair
FROM: Lynn Miyahira on behalf of Public Access to SunScreens (PASS) Coalition
DATE: Friday, November 19, 2021
TIME: 9:00 AM
PLACE: Via videoconference
Re: Bill 135 to prohibit the sale, use, or distribution of non-mineral sunscreens
Position: OPPOSED
Thank you for the opportunity to provide testimony on this important bill. We appreciate the
work of the Maui County Council.
The Public Access to SunScreens (PASS) Coalition is a multi-stakeholder coalition composed of
public health groups, dermatologists, sunscreen manufacturers, and leading advocates for skin
cancer patients. The PASS Coalition opposes this measure as it will create additional barriers for
consumers to access their choice of safe, effective and FDA-approved sunscreens as a skin
cancer prevention tool.
We ask that the Maui County Council hold off on passing Bill 135 or any other legislation on
sunscreen ingredients, until more data on environmental and public health impacts are
available.
The use of sunscreen is an important evidence-based sun-safe practice. It is well known that
utilizing comprehensive sun-safe practices is one of the most effective ways to reduce the risk
of skin cancer, including the regular use of sunscreen, wearing sun protective clothing, hats and
sunglasses, and seeking shade. Skin cancer prevention tools, such as broad-spectrum
sunscreens that protect against both UVA and UVB rays, must be combined with
comprehensive educational tools to ensure consumer awareness of the risks of skin cancer due
to excessive sun exposure.
Hawaii Residents Are at Higher Risk for Skin Cancer
Some notable skin cancer and sun safety behavioral statistics include:
1
Native Hawaiians and other Pacific Islanders suffer from double the melanoma mortality
rate than the State average'
In 2018, more than one in three Hawaii residents surveyed reported having a sunburn in
the last 12 months, nearly double from the previous year'' - and having just five or
more sunburns in your lifetime is known to double your risk for melanoma'"
Researchers have found that just one blistering sunburn in childhood or adolescence
more than doubles a person's chance of developing melanoma later in life'''
Hawaii has one of the highest daily UV index averages in the nation/ On a scale of 0 -
12, Hawaii has over nine months of the year in very-high (8) to extremely high (11) UV
indexes, making it crucial public health issue for residents to have access multiple tools
to protect them from sun exposure
Science Touted by Sunscreen Ban Advocates Is Flawed
Despite the known risk of skin cancer, Hawaii and  ahandful of other jurisdictions have placed
restrictions on the sale of sunscreens based on limited laboratory testing that led policymakers to
believe banning sunscreen would improve coral reef health. The early studies, however, did not fully
consider the complexity of a coral reef system and had scientific limitations. Importantly, findings from
a 2019 study by Dr. Carys Mitchelmore of the University of Maryland contradicts an earlier study by Dr.
Craig Downs that has been widely promoted by advocates of the sunscreen ban. Dr. Mitchelmore's
study uses rigorous methodology and shows actual levels of oxybenzone sampled from sea water in
Hawaii to be 141 times lower than previously stated by Dr. Downs, and 1,020 times below levels
considered toxic to coral.''*
The limited studies that purported to show a link between sunscreen exposure and coral toxicity are
methodologically flawed and should not be used for evidence-based policy making based on EPA data
reliability standards. Subsequent follow-up studies with more rigorous analyses have not replicated the
work by Dr. Downs, and do not support the conclusions.
Congress Has Directed the National Academy of Sciences to Conduct a Comprehensive Study
For that reason, banning sunscreen will have little impact on protecting coral reef. The
overwhelming consensus amongst the scientific community is that coral decline is primarily
caused by rising ocean temperature, ocean acidification, invasive species, land-based source
pollution, water quality issues due to poor wastewater management and other causes. As a
result, the United States Congress directed the National Academy of Sciences (NAS) to evaluate
the latest science available on the correlation between coral reefs and sunscreens and the
potential public health impact of limiting access to sunscreen.
This NAS study, titled "Environmental Impact of Currently Marketed Sunscreens and Potential
Human Impact of Changes in Sunscreen Usage." will conduct an objective review of these issues
by leading scientific experts. The project description is as follows:
2
Concerns have been raised about the potential toxicity of sunscreens to a variety of
marine and fresh\A/ater aquatic organisms, particularly corals. At the same time, there
are concerns that people will use less sunscreen rather than substituting sunscreens
with UV filters that are considered environmentally safe. This study will review the
state of science on use of currently marketed sunscreen ingredients, their fate and
effects in aquatic environments, and the potential public health implications
associated with changes in sunscreen usage.''vii
This study, sponsored by the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency, will examine research
concerning both the environmental and human health impacts of access to sunscreen. This
independent study will evaluate the scientific merit of current science and identify gaps in our
current understanding of coral reef environmental health and human health risks of skin
cancer. All NAS studies involve multiple strategies to reduce bias and to synthesize the best
available science.
NAS Study Should be Completed Before the Council Makes Further Decisions on Consumer
Sunscreen Choice
The conclusion of this NAS study - expected in Spring 2022 - will inform future decisions of
policymakers to ensure access to sunscreens while also protecting the coral reefs. Until this
study is completed, legislation like Bill 135 should be suspended as there are currently
insufficient data to inform a risk/benefit analysis between protecting the marine environment
and protecting the public's health. It is important that the Council wait for unbiased scientific
analysis and consensus.
FDA Advises Continued Use of Currently Marketed Sunscreens
In addition to the lack of peer-reviewed evidence on the environmental impact of sunscreens,
the impact on human health is also still being researched. On September 24, 2021, the Food
and Drug Administration (FDA), which regulates sunscreens as over-the-counter (OTC) drugs for
the prevention of sunburn and skin cancer, issued  afinal order^'" that concluded that, "In the
short term, these new authorities essentially preserve status quo marketing conditions for
these sunscreens" and that "most sunscreens on the market are in compliance with the
deemed final order." To be clear, the FDA's final order did NOT recommend any changes to
currently marketed sunscreens.
Earlier this year, the FDA also posted an article titled, "Shedding More Light on Sunscreen
Absorption'^" that explained that while the FDA was seeking more information on the
absorption levels of sunscreen ingredients, including avobenzone, oxybenzone, octocrylene,
homosalate, octisalate, and octinoxate, it still advises their continued use. The FDA clearly
stated, "Absorption does NOT equal risk - the FDA advises continued use of sunscreens" and
noted that:
3
"The findings in these studies do not mean that the FDA has concluded that any of the
ingredients tested are unsafe for use in sunscreens, nor does the FDA seeking further
information Indicate such. The agency's proposed rule requested additional safety
studies to fill in the current data gaps for these ingredients. The rule also proposed that
two active ingredients {zinc oxide and titanium dioxide) are generally recognized as
safe and effective for use in sunscreens, and additional data was not requested for
them.
Given the recognized public health benefits of sunscreen use, the FDA strongly advises
all Americans to continue to use sunscreens in conjunction with other sun protective
measures (such as protective clothing) as this important rulemaking effort moves
forward."’'
The Hawaii state law signed in July 2018 already eliminated the over-the-counter sale of the
ingredients oxybenzone and octinoxate. Bill 135 would expand this ban to include all non-mineral
sunscreens which and could potentially remove approximately 64% of the sunscreens currently
available in the United States from being sold in Maui.
On average, currently marketed mineral sunscreens can cost up to 30% more than other
sunscreens and this proposed bill could significantly reduce consumer choice of and access to
sunscreen in Hawaii. It is important to remember that sunscreen is not only used in the ocean,
but whenever people are outdoors doing activities such as hiking, golfing, walking, running,
cycling or working outside. This puts Hawaii residents at greater risk for skin cancer with only
limited peer-reviewed scientific evidence on sunscreen ingredients and its impact on
environmental and human health.
Again, we ask that the Council hold off on passing Bill 135, or any other bill on sunscreen
ingredients, until more data on environmental and public health impacts are available.
If the CounciTs Intention is to pass this bill now, may we ask the Council consider an
extension of the effective date so doctors, healthcare providers and pharmacies can figure
out how they will handle sunscreen prescriptions. There are many unanswered questions and
no precedence on how sunscreen prescriptions would be implemented. Ensuring access to
sunscreens is a public health imperative - especially for skin cancer survivors who have a
higher risk of developing further skin cancers.
If you have any questions about the PASS Coalition or the content of this testimony, please feel
free to contact me at imivahira@iQ360inc.com.
Mahalo you for the opportunity to testify.
Sincerely,
Lynn Miyahira
Public Access to SunScreens (PASS) Coalition

IYou don't often get email from kelli@xmission.com. Learn why this is important
Dear Sirs and Madams,
My name is Kelli Lundgren. I have been a volunteer at Ahihi-Kina'u Natural Area Reserve since 2014. In the past five
years, since scientific data first offered evidence that endocrine inhibitors used in many sunscreens stifle coral growth
and interrupt fish reproductivity in even the smallest exposures, 1 have been educating visitors on how they can help
present damage to the reef.
Here is what I have learned bv helping educate sometimes up to 150 people a dav:
1. Almost every person or family I speak to wants to help protect Hawaii's reefs. It's a positive conversation.
2. Reef visitors pull out their "reef safe" sunscreen tube/spray to say that they are helping. And indeed, sometimes they
are using safe sunblock (zinc oxide or titanium dioxide). We all smile. But, many times I have to reply: of course you want
to help the reef by buying "reef safe," but this spray is not reef safe. It's a marketing term only. The FDA does not have a
definition for "reef safe". It can be used in any instance on any product. And it is used vigorously by most sunscreen
manufacturers. Visitors become concerned, mostly because they want to do the right thing.
3. As you know, "Oxybenzone" and "Octinoxate" have officially been banned in Hawaii. Still, ten or more other
endocrine inhibitors proven dangerous to reefs by scientific evidence (chemicals such as Avobenzone, Homosalate,
Octocrylene, etc.), are being used widely in sprays and lotions. It's a catch-up game for science to get these chemicals off
the Hawaiian islands and anywhere close to any of the world's reefs.
4. In the meantime, Hawaii's reefs are stressed from sometimes 2000 people a day heading into one reef: Ahihi-Kina'u,
Kapalua, Honolua, Maluaka, Olowalu. One teaspoon of any of these chemicals can toxify six Olympic sized swimming
pools of ocean. At Ahihi, we have 600 to 800 people a day heading into one of the most beautiful reefs on this planet.
You can imagine the toxicity. Animal life gets hurt.
5. Toxic sunscreen chemicals will even damage reefs from hotel rooms, homes, and use anywhere on island. I have to
tell visitors it matters not just when you go into the ocean or sit on a beach. To help, don't use it at all on Island. It gets
into the wastewater system and enters the ocean.
6. The visitor experience wading through retail shelves for the right sunscreen is absolutely confusing. They are willing to
go back into a store to do the right thing. They have to look past "reef safe." They have to read six point small print
under active ingredients. They have to find the 20% of actually safe products by using research skills. It's hard when it's
not your expertise.
Here's the positive news if chemical sunscreens were banned from the perspective of a visitor:
Any visitor could walk into any store on island and feel good that what is available on the shelf is safe for the reef. Most
visitors want this. That's why they have been buying the misguided reef safe labeled sunscreens. Now they could rest
assured they are buying mineral sunblock.
1
Here*s the positive news for sunscreen/sunblock manufacturers:
Almost all sunscreen manufacturers also produce and sell mineral-only sunblocks. Instead of selling 80% chemicals and
20% minerals, they now sell 100% minerals in Maui County. Only their product mix changes. Not their revenue.
Here's the positive news for Hawaii's reef life:
The reefs will heal, and can focus on protecting themselves from other stresses.
I cannot express enough how much visitors appreciate the concept of only mineral sunblock availability on Maui. It
makes a vacationer's job easier while they are trying to do the right thing. I hear this over and over when talking to
people.
It's change, but also a win/win for all.
Best Regards,
Kelli Lundgren
Ahihi-Kina'u Natural Area Reserve Volunteer

STATEMENT OF THE ILWU LOCAL 142 ON COUNTY COMMUNICATION 21-130
Friday, November 19,2021; 9:00 a.m
Dear Maui County Council:
The International Longshore & Warehouse Union, Local 142 {"ILWU Local 142") opposes the proposed
bill endorsed by CR 21-130 in its current form. The bill as written, will negatively impact our members.
Specifically, our union would like to see the following changes made to the bill:
1. We object to the use of both "lodging capacity" and "structural footprint" language in Section
19.98.040 and suggest replacing it with "transient accommodation units" so union jobs relating
to redeveloping properties or expanding restaurants, lobbies, grounds and other projects that
do not increase the number of units can still proceed.
2. We request clarification that the moratorium ends upon the passage of the first piece of
legislation that adopts any recommendation of the temporary investigative group. The current
language in Section 19.98.050 of the bill uses "implementation" of "recommendations." This is
vague and subject to different interpretation. The trigger to end the moratorium must be clear.
Limiting redevelopment that does not increase the number of units Is not consistent with the stated
purpose of the moratorium. It is contrary to the Countywide Policy Plan, inconsistent with the general
plan and is vague. The bill needs to allow for renovation and redevelopment that do not increase the
number of units.
Thank you for your consideration of this testimony.
Sincerely,
ILWU Local 142
Maui Division
V/
Roberto Andrion Jr.
Maui Division DirectorRA:jkn

Aloha Maui County Council,
I would like to fully support Maui Bill 135. This bill will be critical in conserving Maui’s coral
reefs which are already beleaguered from stresses such as climate change and runoff. Removing
the stress of sunscreen pollution can increase the resiliency of Maui’s coral reefs to these global
and local stressors, and may be the necessary step to allow the reefs to begin recovering.
Everyone saw how clear the water was, and how the fish and corals returned during the COVID
lockdown of 2020. This tabula rasa event is a demonstration of what Maui’s water could be
without the sheen of sunscreen pollution.
I am specifically testifying against adversarial comments and arguments that have been directed
at Maui Bill 135 from some members of the sunscreen industry, including the American
Academy of Dermatology Association (AADA).
1. The AADA claims that mineral filters are “less effective filters.” This is blatantly false
information. Zinc Oxide is a superior UVA filter, and absorbs in the entire UVA
wavelength spectrum, while avobenzone absorbance precipitously drops offs before and
after 357 nm. ZnO has a level absorption across the entire UVA spectrum. Furthermore,
avobenzone is extremely unstable, especially during application, and readily degrades,
leaving the user susceptible to sunscreen abuse (thinking they are protected, but they are
not being protected). A good scientific source that rebuffs the AADA statement is:
https://onlinclibrarv.vvilev.eom/doi/full/10.l 111/phpp.12439
Even a major sunscreen trade journal advocates for ZnO sunscreen formulations (written
by BASF, a major supplier of mineral and petrochemical UV filters).
hUps://www.happi.com/issucs/2020-06-01/vicw_features/bcst-practi ces-for-rormulating-
sunscreen-with-zno/
2. Avobenzone requires OCTOCRYLENE as a product stabilizer. Octocrylene has been
proven to breakdown into BENZOPHENONE (in the sunscreen bottle), a known
carcinogen, endocrine disruptor, and Monsanto-patented herbicide. Octocrylene causes
developmental toxicity in fish, metabolic toxicity in coral, and could potentially cause
bleaching in coral (it is a patented herbicide that could attack the coral’s algal symbiont).
Lawsuits have been filed in the state of California under Proposition 65 that all
octocrylene products need to be labeled as containing a substance that is a recognized
carcinogen and reproductive toxicant.
3. In June 2021, the European Commission’s Scientific Committee on Consumer Safety
provided an opinion on HOMOSALATE as being so toxic to humans that it must not be
used above a concentration of 0.5% in sunscreens. Currently, in the U.S., homosalate is
being used at 15% - 30x over what is considered safe. You can access their full report
here:
1 I P a g e
https://ec.curopa.eu/health/sitcs/dcfault/filcs/scientific committees/consumer safcty/docs
/sees o 244.pdf
4. Petrochemical sunscreens have a history of failing to protect against skin cancer. This can
happen for a number of reasons - faulty formulation, sunscreen abuse, over reliance of
UVB filters and not enough UVA protection. A recent scientific paper called out these
factors of why sunscreens, and especially petrochemical sunscreen formulation, can fail
to protect against skin cancer.

5. The U.S. Centers for Disease Control specifically state that to reduce the risk of cancer, a
person should:
Stay in the shade.
Wear clothing that covers your arms and legs.
Wear a hat with a wide brim to shade your face, head, ears, and neck.
Wear sunglasses that wrap around and block both UVA and UVB rays.
Use a broad spectrum sunscreen with a sun protection factor (SPF) of 15 or higher.

Notice Bulleted Point #5. This is the last recommendation by the CDC to reduce the risk of
skin cancer. Also note that it does not make the distinction between mineral sunscreen and
petrochemical sunscreen. It just says, “use a broad spectrum” sunscreen, and a combination
of Zn0/Ti02 using a non-acidic formula provides exactly a “broad spectrum protection.59
6. It should also be noted that melanoma rates are on the rise. If sunscreen protected against
melanoma, and more people are being encouraged to use sunscreen, why don’t we see levels
decrease? You can’t say more people are outside now that back in the 1920s, because prior to
the 1970s, most of the population worked outside, and not indoors. Melanoma rates and
sunscreen usage rates see increasing and parallel tracking. The obvious hypothesis to put
forth is whether sunscreen use is causing an increase in the rates of melanoma because of the
many reasons why sunscreens fail to protect.
7. Several physician groups claim that they have the patient and public welfare in the best
interest, but that has not always been the case. In 1939, the first scientific paper was
published by Ochsner and DeBakey showed that smoking could be the dominant cause of
lung pathologies and lung cancer. It took 25 years before the U.S. Surgeon General issued a
report recognizing this causal link. During that time, many physicians fully endorsed tobacco
smoking as safe. So much so that there were cigarette advertisements in medical journals up
until 1964, when the Surgeon General admitted this terrible travesty.

Like smoking, sunscreen pollution is a situation where the science and educated legislators
are out in front of the issue. It may take time for the medical profession to catch up, but the
preponderance of the science in the public literature is that petrochemical sunscreens as they are
currently formulated in the U.S. may pose both a public health and environmental threat.
With second-hand cigarette smoke, you can still be afflicted with smoking diseases. And like
cigarette smoke, sunscreen pollution by petrochemical sunscreen filters may pose a health risk to
pregnant persons, children, and cancer patients. There are a number of individuals and families
who are concerned about getting into sunscreen polluted waters. Two U.S. FDA studies showed
that oxybenzone, avobenzone, octocrylene, and octinoxate are readily absorbed through the skin,
and some UV filters, like oxybenzone, can persist in a person’s blood stream for more than 2
weeks at concentrations above the FDA safety action level.

8. Many professional associations and product-protection lobby firms have made a statement
such as:
“The FDA’s conclusion from recent studies on sunscreen ingredient absorption “supports the
need for further studies to determine the clinical significance of these findings.” FDA further
stated that “these findings do not indicate that individuals should refrain from the use of
sunscreen.”
This is technically correct, but egregiously misconstrued.
(A) The U.S. FDA is acting incorrectly. According to the U.S. Federal Food, Drug, and
Cosmetic Act of 1938, regulated drugs need to be proved to be SAFE and EFFECTIVE
before commercialization is permitted. Sunscreens are drugs. The FDA is acting
incorrectly by allowing petrochemical sunscreens to be used in Over-the-Counter
sunscreen drugs. The proper protocol is for FDA to prohibit the sale of any sunscreen that
is not Category I, Generally Recognized as Safe and Effective (GRASE). Not following
this protocol puts the general public in danger. The FDA proved that petrochemical
sunscreens (at least four of them) are readily absorbed into the skin and contaminates the
whole body. We know breast milk can be highly contaminated by oxybenzone (the first
public study was published in 1992 by the Germans). There are a number of studies
demonstrating that oxybenzone and other petrochemicals can cause cancer cell
proliferation, can cause cancer (National Toxicology Program), are mutagenic and cause
other forms of genotoxic and chromosomal damage. There are a number of studies
showing oxybenzone as an estrogenic endocrine disruptor, octinoxate as a thyroid
endocrine disruptor, and octocrylene/benzophenone as an endocrine disruptor.
Basically, what the FDA is supposed to legally do is stop the selling of all Category
3-GRASE sunscreen products, and demand industry provide the safety and efficacy data
so that an assessment can be done.
Flow this statement by the FDA should be correctly interpreted is that industry MUST
provide additional studies, because there is no proof of whether these chemicals are safe
or effective. Industry has been non-compliant for over 40 years. We don’t know if
sunscreen causes melanoma (or prevents skin cancer), but industry NEEDS to produce
this data so that we (the public) and the FDA can make that decision.
(B) “these findings do not indicate that individuals should refrain from the use of sunscreen.”
What this sentence does NOT say is that you should continue to use Category 3-GRASE
sunscreen products (all the petrochemical UV filters). It just says “... the use of
This “use sunscreen” statement SHOULD be interpreted as using Category 1-sunscreen.
GRASE sunscreen products, zinc oxide and titanium dioxide. Should you really interpret
this as the FDA recommending the public to use an untested, unproven SAFE and
unproven EFFECTIVE sunscreen formulation/product?
9. Professional associations, medical doctors, and product-protection firms have been making
this statement to legislatures since 2017:
“Sunscreen ingredients have been in use for almost 50 years without any reported
systemic adverse side effects.”
5 I Page
This is blatantly a false statement. Systemic, adverse side effects regarding petrochemical
sunscreens have been documented in the medical and scientific literature for the past 20 years. In
fact, the American Contact Dermatitis Society made four of the Category 3-GRASE
petrochemical UV filters - oxybenzone, benzophenone, dioxybenzone, sulisobenzone - the 2014
Contact Allergen of the Year.
https://wvvw.mdedgc.eom/dermatolotiv/article/80980/psoriasis/bcnzophcnoncs-namcd-2014-
contact-allergen-vear
Oxybenzone, since 2012, was associated with endometriosis by independent science groups:
https://pubs.acs.oru/doi/abs/10.1021 /cs204415a
https://www.scicnccdirect.coiTi/scicnce/article/abs/Dii/SOO 13935120312391
https://www.scicnccdircct.com/scicnce/article/abs/pi i/SOO 15028216613894
Both oxybenzone and its primary metabolite, benzophenone-1, have been known to cause
cancer cell proliferation (of a number of different types of cancer) for more than a decade:
https://link.sprinHcr.com/article/10.1007/s 10565-016-9368-3
https://ioiirnals.plos.orH/plosonc/articlc?id=lQ. I371/iournal.ponc.0060567
hllps://www.scicnccdircct.coin/scicncc/articlc/pii/S 1382668915000095
https://wwvv.tandlbnlinc.eom/doi/abs/l 0.1080/15287394,2015.1010464
https://w\vw.scicnccdirect.com/scicncc/article/abs/pii/S0300483X 13000085
https://www.scienccdirect.eom/scicnce/article/abs/nii/S0006295209010624
10. Testimony from product-protection associations and firms will try to manufacture doubt
regarding the dozens upon dozens of scientific papers that show that many of these
petrochemical UV filters pose a danger to ecological systems, including coral reefs. These
testimonies usually only cite a single published paper for their arguments:
Mitchelmore CS, Burns, EE, Conway A, Heyes A, Davies lA. A critical review of organic
ultraviolet filter exposure, hazard, and risk to corals. Environ Toxicol Chem. 2020 (00);00:1-
21.
It is highly probable for an objective and rational scientist to extensively critique the
arguments and statements of this paper, demonstrating the invalidity of many of their premises,
as well as the fallaciousness of their arguments’ conclusions. And I would be more than happy to
do that with a County Council member. But I would put forth the argument that whether
intended or not by the authors, the consequence of this paper is the Manufacturing of Doubt
about the veracity and validity of the scientific papers they attack - a tactic used by the product-
protection industry for the past 100 years, as it was used in the wars regarding tobacco, leaded
gas, glyphosate, talcum powder, polyfiuoroalkyl substances, climate change, etc.. To learn more
of this tactic, please enjoy reading the following sources:
https://www.scicncedircct.eom/sciencc/article/abs/pii/S0095069617303273
https://www.deHruytcr.eom/document/doi/10.1515/reveh-2019-0004/htinl
6 I P a g e
https://papcrs.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm7abstract id=3097156
https://\v\v\v.nevvscientist.com/article/mg20627606-200-living-in-denial-how-
corporations-manufacture-doubt/
This paper by Mitcheimore et al. was wholly funded and written directly or through financial
associations by persons in the product-protection industry - the Personal Care Product Council.
The sole purpose of the Personal Care Product Council is to assert and protect the interests of
their clients - those being many of the corporate members that manufacture and sell Category 3-
GRASE sunscreen products. This begs the question of the motivation and intent of both
referencing this paper in testimony, as well as the motivation to have published this paper.
Independent scientists, conservationists, as well as the tourism industry applauds your
audaciousness and integrity in trying to manage the potential adverse effects associated with
sunscreen pollution through Maui Bill 135.
Furthermore, whether the sunscreen industry admits this or not, your initiative and resolve
will make the sunscreen industry better. The U.S. Sunscreen Industry can be perceived as a
“fossilized dinosaur”; its formulations with its “8 UV filter ingredients” have not changed in the
past 60 years. They have not looked for safer or more ecologically sustainable ingredients or
formulations. Maui Bill 135 will breathe new air into the industry by forcing them to innovate
and re-examine their values. Passing this bill will place a demand on industry to pursue
ecological sustainability for their products. Twenty years from now, because of the council’s
resolution, society may have a dozen new UV filter ingredients that are safer for people and coral
reefs.
Sincerely,
Craig Downs, PhD.

Subject: Mineral sunscreens are only Safe and EFFECTIVE (GRASE)
Only mineral sunscreens are GRASE:
This is stated of the U.S. FDA website as of November 16, 2021
● Active ingredients: The deemed final order considers sunscreens containing i6 sunscreen active
ingredients to be GRASE, consistent with the 1999 stayed (not in effect) sunscreen monograph. Based
on new data and changed conditions since issuance of the 1999 monograph, the proposed order
proposes GRASE status for sunscreens containing zinc oxide and titanium dioxide; not GRASE status
for sunscreens containing aminobenzoic acid (PABA) and trolamine salicylate, because the evidence
shows that these sunscreens are not GRASE due to safety issues; and not GRASE status for sunscreens
containing cinoxate, dioxybenzone, ensulizole, homosalate, meradimate, octinoxate, octisalate,
octocr>Tene, padimate 0, sulisobenzone, oxybenzone, and avobenzone, because additional data is
needed to show that these sunscreens are GRASE.

order-and-proposed-order-over-counter-sunscreen

Request for Amendment of Bill 133:19.65.030
Email confirmation from Ryan.jpeg

IYou don't often get email from rsbeatty@yahoo.com. Learn why this is important
November 18, 2021
Request for amendment of Bill 133: 19.65.030 to include provision for the transfer of STVR permit from one
spouse to another in the event of divorce.
Testimony of Roberta Beatty
I am requesting an amendment to Bill 133:19.65.030 to include a provision for the transfer of an STVR permit
between spouses in the event of divorce. In April 2019, after three years of working with the County, I was
granted an STVR for my property in Hana. Unfortunately, my planner, Ryan Quigless, made an error and
issued the permit in my husband's name and not mine. In writing, I had instructed the plannerto put the
permit in my name, but he failed to do so. My husband and I are now getting a divorce, and I will be the sole
owner of our Hana property. I very much want to continue living in Hana and running the STVR business that I
started and have been managing since receiving my STVR permit.
Sincerely,
Roberta Beatty OCj

Aloha Council Members,
We mentioned information during the recent Council meeting that Council Member Kama had previously provided
regarding occupation and income for Maui County.
We were able to locate the information, entitled "Long Term Occupational Projections, 2016-2026 for Maui MSA
(attached for your convenience and review.)
We checking the website and were able to find a more current report and provide the portion headed Occupational
Employment and Wage Data, May 2020 - Maui MSA (relevant portion attached for your convenience and review.)
We hope you will reconsider the AMI range that this information will impact in the Comprehensive Affordable Housing
Plan: Income Group Distribution for Residential Workforce Housing Units (AH-14(5)) by retaining the above-moderate
income group.
You are always welcome to call or email me with any questions or if we may be of further assistance.●'

Opposition to Bill 135
Dear Maui County Council Members,
Mahalo for your concern about maintaining the beauty of Hawaii. With that said, my opposition to Bill
135 and my concern is that mineral only sunscreens would result in less access for the public that would
result with negative health outcomes in the long-run. Only mineral ingredients in sunscreens may result
with more expensive sunscreens/sunblock for sale that would result with less people using necessary
sun protection. This is a equity issue- most people might not be able to afford more expensive
sunscreens. In future years we may find a higher diagnosis of various types of skin cancer.
Mahalo,
Cynthia Au

Honolulu, HI 96814

November 17, 2021
Re: STRONG SUPPORT OF BILL 21-135: A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE ESTABLISHING
CHAPTER 20.42, MAUI COUNTY CODE, TO RPOHIBIT THE SALE, USE, OR DISTRIBUTION
OF NON-MINERAL SUNSCREENS
Aloha Maui County Council,
On behalf of the Board of Directors of Friends of Hanauma Bay, mahalo for the opportunity to
testify in strong support of Bill 21-135. Maui County led Hawai’i in the effort to ban chemical
sunscreens in 2017, and we are pleased to add our support for Bill 21 -135 which also prohibits
their use.
This is the next important step to help ensure public health and the health of our fragile marine
environments, further emphasized by the FDA’s recent proposal to classify all non-mineral
organic UV filters found in OTC sunscreens as Category II - Not Generally Recognized as Safe
and Effective due to lack of evidence of their safety and effectiveness.
The Personal Care Product Industry has had more than 40 years to prove the safety and
effectiveness of products containing non-mineral UV filters, yet still hasn’t done so, because
they simply aren’t safe and effective. Enough is enough.
We applaud Maui County residents and the Maui County Council for your courageous
leadership on this issue, and look forward to seeing similar sucessful efforts throughout our
State.
Mahalo for considering our testimony. Please pass Bill 21-135!
Sincerely,
Lisa Bishop
President

receivedTestimony from the Hawaii Skin Cancer Coalition Against
im NOV 17 PN 12: 04Bill Number 135, "A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE ESTABLISHING CHAPTER 20.42,
MAUI COUNTY CODE, TO PROHIBIT THE SALE, USE, OR
MINERAL SUNSCREENS" DISTRIBUJIQI^Cg^t^ryT^
CSOUNTY CLERK
To the Honorable Chair and Members of the Maui County Council:
The members of the Hawaii Skin Cancer Coalition voice our strong opposition to Bill
#135, “A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE ESTABLISHING CHAPTER 20.42, MAUI
COUNTY CODE, TO PROHIBIT THE SALE, USE, OR DISTRIBUTION OF NON
MINERAL SUNSCREENS.”
While the intent of this bill is to prevent the decline of our precious coral reefs, it may
in fact have the opposite effect and promote coral decline for the following reasons:
1) Recent studies have identified that mineral sunscreens and the physical
residue they leave in our ocean may cause more damage to coral reefs and are
also damaging to marine life.
Additionally, this bill is premature as:
2) The EPA has convened a national committee of scientific experts to
examine the ecological and human effects of sunscreens. The committee’s
recommendations are expected to be released in Spring 2022. The ban may
countermand the findings of this national effort to examine the effects of
sunscreen components and their constituent chemicals.
3) The ban may inadvertently create an illegal market for sunscreen products
and booster disingenuous efforts to profit from illegally conferring reef-safety
status on marketed sunscreens.
Finally:
4) The bill will remarkably reduce the effectiveness of currently marketed
sunscreens to prevent sunburn, premature aging and skin cancers. Currently,
skin cancer in the most common cancer type in the US with more than 5
million cases diagnosed each year for an average annual treatment cost of
$8.1 billion.
The Hawaii Skin Cancer Coalition is a collaborative effort between concerned local
organizations and businesses including, the University of Hawai’i Cancer Center,
American Cancer Society, Hawaii Pathologists’ Laboratory, the Friends of the
University of Hawai’i Cancer Center, the Hawaii Dermatological Society,
Kaiser Permanente, Kuakini Health System, the Hawaii Lifeguard Association,
Queen’s Healthcare Plan, the Hawaii Ophthalmological Society. All of these
organizations share a common goal to help prevent skin cancer.
The Hawaii Skin Cancer Coalition’s mission is to provide clear, concise messages
on skin cancer prevention and early detection for both the public and health
professionals based upon current and accurate information.
REFERENCES;
Fel, JP., Lacherez, C.. Bensetra, A. et al. Photochemical response of the
scleractinian coral Stylophora pistillata to some sunscreen ingredients. Coral
Reefs 38, 109-122 (2019). https://doi.org/10.1007/s00338-018-01759-4

Support for Bill 135

Dear Maui County Council,
I am writing to you today to express my support for Bill 135:
People don’t realize how bad the effects of non reef safe sunscreen is. Up to 6,000 tons of sunscreen
are estimated to wash into coral reefs around the globe each year. Most of that is full of Homosalate
and Parabens, which aren’t only bad for the environment, but also bad for you, with inhaling non reef
sunscreen is even worse than it seeping into your skin. In fact, says Craig A. Downs, Ph.D., executive
director of the nonprofit Haereticus Environmental Laboratory, though oxybenzone and octinoxate are
the most widely studied, there are several other chemicals used in sunscreens and other personal
care products that research suggests might be an environmental threat. This is why I fully support Bill
135.
Sincerely,
Nicole Critchlow
7th Grade, Kihei Charter School

In Support of MauKs Bill 135 (2021) to Prohibit the sale, use or distribution of non-mineral sunscreens
Joseph C. DiNardo, MS - Toxicologist
November 18, 2021
I would like to thank the Council of the County of Maui for the opportunity to comment on this very
important environmental and human health bill relating to non-mineral sunscreens (organic sunscreen
actives). The following comments are based on my experience with product development, regulatory
compliance as well as pre-clinical and clinical safety testing with some environmental testing of OTC
sunscreen actives and formulations dating back to 1976.
Below are the references to a number of scientific publications, citizen petitions and critiques on
studies that my colleagues and I have published demonstrating the toxicity of various organic
sunscreen actives currently under FDA scrutiny. Not only are these chemicals toxic to the environment
but also clearly toxic to human life and should not be allowed for sale.
Additionally, I would like to reiterate that the U.S. National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration
(NOAA) has already recognized that several sunscreen actives not only harm coral but also cause
damage to algae, mussels, sea urchins, fish and dolphins.
https://oceanscrvice.noaa.gov/news/sunscreen-corals.html

In Support of Maui County Bill 135 (2021)
To:
OFFICE OF THE
COUNTY CLERKSubject:
You don't often get email from ferguson,ali@gmail.com. Learn why this is important
)ear Honorable Maui County Councilmembers,
I am a frequent and long time visitor to the Hawaiian Islands. I am in strong support of Bill 135 prohibiting the sale,
use, or distribution of non-mineral sunscreens that have questionable effects on the health of humans and marine life.
On September 24, 2021, the FDA issued a proposed order concerning nonprescription sunscreen drug products. In
the proposed order, two mineral products zinc oxide and titanium dioxide are deemed generally recognized as safe
and effective (GRASE), and fourteen products are deemed NOT GRASE. Of the fourteen products, twelve products
do not currently contain sufficient data to support positive GRASE classification. The twelve products that require
additional data are avobenzone, cinoxate, dioxybenzone, ensulizole, homosalate, meradimate, octinoxate, octisalate,
octocrylene, oxybenzone, padimate 0, and sulisobenzone.
It is in the people’s best interest that we apply the Precautionary Principle which asserts that the burden of proof for
potentially harmful actions by industry or government rests on the assurance of safety and that when there are threats
of serious damage, scientific uncertainty must be resolved in favor of prevention.
Sincerely,
Alison Ferguson
1078 Peninsula St
Ventura CA 93001

Bill 135 — My written testimony
RECEIVEDTo:
W\ NOV 17 PH |: 02Subject:
OFriCE OF THE
COUNTY CLERKIYou don't often get email from bjfogg@stanford.edu. Learn why this is important
I'm a resident of Maui. I surf in south Maui about 150 times a year, usually wearing sunscreen.
1 strongly support the proposal to prohibit non-mineral sunscreens on our island.
In addition, I believe we need to be clearer about which sunscreens are actually "reef safe" as opposed to "reef
friendly" or other confusing terms.
Here's my story of failure ...
I have a Ph.D. from Stanford, and I'm a good researcher. I've tried to buy and use only "reef safe" sunscreen. But this
week I learned I've made mistakes.
Over the last year or so, I purchased 12 brands of sunscreen. I got them all out today and looked at the ingredients
carefully. I was bewildered to learn that 5 of the 12 products were NOT reef safe. 1 thought they ALL were. (In fact,
one brand I bought at the surf shop says "reef safe" on it but yet contains 7% octinoxate.)
Please take steps to limit the sale of sunscreens that are not reef safe. Also, if there's a way to do so, let's stop
people from bringing damaging sunscreens to Maui when they visit.
Thank you.
BJ Fogg, PhD
Adjunct Faculty, Stanford University
bifoeg@stanford.edu
Maui Resident, living at 4955 Makena Road, Kihei

Kalana O Maui Building, 8*^ floor

RE: OPPOSITION - Legislation Banning the Sale, Use, and Distribution of Non-Mineral
Sunscreens (Bill No.135)
Dear Chair Lee.
On behalf ofthe Consumer Healthcare Products Association (CHPA), the national trade
association representing the leading manufacturers of over-the-counter (OTC) medications,
dietary supplements, and consumer medical devices, I am writing to express strong opposition
to (Bill No.135) - a proposed ordinance seeking to prohibit the sale. use. or distribution of non
mineral sunscreen.
CHPA is the leading voice fighting to ensure that Americans have access to safe and effective
OTC medications to get well, stay healthy and - as the case with sunscreens - prevent serious
illness. Our mission is to empower self-care by preserving and expanding choice and
availability of consumer healthcare products, including both mineral and non-mineral
sunscreens, so that consumers can live happier, healthier lives through responsible seif-care.
Unfortunately, removing consumer access to the most popular safe and effective skin cancer
preventing sunscreens on the market today - as described in the proposed ordinance - runs
contrary to these ideals and will adversely impact the health and welfare of Maui residents and
its visitors.
Sunscreens Are Safe. Effective and Save Lives
Sunscreen ingredients currently approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) are
commonly used to block the full range of ultraviolet rays that are linked to skin cancer - one of
the most common, yet preventable forms of cancer in the world according to the World
Health Organization (WHO). Eliminating sunscreen options for consumers needlessly increases
the risk of skin cancer for residents and visitors of Maui. In fact, the American Cancer Society
estimates that melanoma will be one ofthe leading causes of new cancer cases in Hawaii in
2021.
The State of Hawaii remains the only American state to have banned the sale of sunscreens
containing oxybenzone and octinoxate. Needlessly expanding this ban in Maui to include all
non-mineral sunscreens inaccurately depicts sunscreen ingredients as harmful to coral reefs
and other marine life; a position that is contrary to the scientific consensus that rising sea
temperatures as a result of global warming are the primary cause of coral decline, and that
global warming, land pollution, and other human activities are the primary causes of coral
bleaching around the world.
1625 Eye Street. NW. Suite 600 I Washington. DC 20006 1 Tel: 202.A29.9260 I chpa.org
Consumer Healthcare Products Association
Opposition to Proposed Sunscreen Ordinance
November 18, 2021 - Page 2 of 3
Given the decades of safe and effective use by humans and the lack of convincing scientific
evidence that sunscreens are responsible for environmental and marine decline, we strongly
oppose this proposed legislation. Consumer access to sunscreen products containing a broad
variety of ingredients, especially in a state with the highest rate of melanoma cases attributed
to UV exposure, is a matter of public health. For these reasons, we oppose passage of CR 21-113.
Food and Drug Administration (FDA) Will Evaluate The Potential Environmental Impact of
Non-Mineral Sunscreens
FDA has noted that they intend to prepare an Environmental Impact Statement (EIS) under
the National Environmental Policy Act to evaluate the potential environmental effects of
revised conditions for marketing certain sunscreen products for OTC use without prior
approval of a new drug application. In preparing the EiS, FDA must complete a record of
decision stating the full decision, identifying and discussing the alternatives considered, state
whether all practical means to avoid or minimize the environmental harm have been adopted,
and summarize the program for monitoring and enforcing the practical means adopted.
There is no mandate that certain decisions be made (or not made) based on the EIS. just that
the impact and alternatives be discussed.
Sunscreen Bans by Local Government in Hawaii May Be Illegal
In 2017, the Maui County Department of the Corporation Counsel advised the Maui Council of
legal issues that may apply with proposed ordinances seeking to ban specific sunscreens.
Specifically, the Department of Corporation Counsel suggested that such an ordinance may. in
fact, be preempted by both State and Federal law. Additionally, the Department warned the
Council that a local sunscreen ban may also conflict with the federal Commerce Clause, and
therefore could trigger a legal challenge. The Hawaii Revised Statutes (HRS) broadly
authorizes the Hawaii Department of Land and Natural Resources (DLNR) to regulate and
oversee "near-shore waters." Since Maui County’s powers are derived from the State of Hawai'i,
HRS, and the amended Charter of Maui County in 1982, a sunscreen sales ban is likely invalid.
Sunscreen regulation in Hawai'i, therefore, should be left to the Hawai'i legislature as it was
when the county contemplated a similar ban of oxybenzone and octinoxate containing
sunscreens a few years ago.
Conclusion
CHPA respectfully requests you oppose any policy that bans the sale, use, or distribution of
non-mineral sunscreens. A decision of this magnitude deserves a deliberative discussion and
examination of all potential consequences - including the health of Maui residents and visitors.
Thank you for your consideration and please feel free to contact me directly with any
questions.
Respectfully submitted,
Carlos 1. Gutierrez
Vice President, State & Local Government Affairs
Consumer Healthcare Products Association
Consumer Healthcare Products Association
Opposition to Proposed Sunscreen Ordinance

November 17, 2021
Dear Maui County Council
I am writing to you today to express my support for Bill 135. It is a very serious situation.
Levels of chemicals in ‘Ahihi Bay have been found at 868 parts per trillion, or fourteen times the “safe”
levels for coral to survive the natural area reserve states. Oxybenzone, octocrylene and octinoxate
are the primary sunscreen ingredients of concern. Zinc and titanium dioxide are mineral ingredients
that are good for your body and the coral reefs by the Food and Drug Administration. Bill 2571
banned only two of the many ingredients that harm the reefs. Companies making non reef safe
sunscreen products falsely advertise that they are “reef friendly” when they state that there is no
oxybenzone in their ingredients. They might not have oxybenzone in the sunscreen, but that doesn’t
apply to other toxic chemicals. Not only are these toxic chemicals bad for the environment, but they
can be bad for yourself. Tourists might go to a shop and spot a “reef friendly” sunscreen and think
about how much they want to help the reefs and blindly hurt them. That is why I am in strong favor for
supporting Bill 135.
Sincerely,
Madilyn Hays
Kihei Charter School, 7th grade

November 16, 2021
Honorary Chair and Members:
I am Curtis Higashiyama, Employee Relations and Government Affairs Manager representing ABC Stores.
We are asking for an extension of Bill 135 beyond its effective date so doctors, healthcare providers and
pharmacies can determine how sunscreen prescriptions will be handled. Among some of the questions
are:
● What will be the structure for doctors to prescribe sunscreen?
● Will pharmacies carry the product behind the counter?
●  Regulating prescription medications or over the counter drugs: Maui County's jurisdiction?
●  Health insurance companies: Will the prescription for sunscreen be recognized when the FDA
considers it an over the counter drug?
We are also requesting the following:
● The Council go back to the original wording that only banned oxybenzone and octinoxate, similar
to the statewide ban that started on January 1, 2021.
●  Further movement be put on hold until the National Academy of Science (NAS) completes their
review of scientific literature of sunscreen's impact on both environmental and human health.
The NAS should publish a report in Spring 2022 and will give decision makers guidance on how to
approach sunscreen rulings.
Following are advisories/ recommendations by the FDA and DOH:
● The FDA recommended no changes to currently marketed sunscreens. The FDA is studying
chemical UV filters in sunscreens, but does not recommend banning them for use.
●  In a correspondence from the Hawaii DOH dated August 2, 2021: from a skin cancer/ human
health perspective, it is NOT advisable to limit sunscreens to only zinc/ titanium.
Through 37 plus years in Waikiki I observed a need for sun care products, all types, not only zinc/
titanium. There will be a huge problem with satisfying the needs of those who are local and those visiting
us if availability will only be at pharmacies. I personally do not see many pharmacies in resort areas or
even in urban areas.
We would like to continue servicing our guests both locally and from abroad by providing them with
choices in needed sun protection during their stay in Hawaii. As we who live here know, activities
requiring sunscreen protection are not only for swimming, but also for other outdoor activities such as
running, hiking, golfing, yardwork... Let's help minimize potential sun related health hazards for our
people and guests of Hawaii due to limited choice and limited availability.
Honorary Chair and Members, again we ask that an extension is moved for Bill 135.
Thank you for allowing me the opportunity to share this testimony. OC C39
Curtis Higashiyama: Employee Relations & Government Affairs Manager C

Concerns involving the health care delivery system:
●  There is no structure set up for the prescription of sunscreens.
●  The jurisdiction of regulating prescription medications or over the counter drugs is not dear.
●  Unclear how the health insurance companies will recognize a prescription for sunscreen when
the FDA recognizes it as an over-the -counter drug.
We are also requesting the following:
●  The Council go back to the original wording that only banned oxybenzone and octinoxate, similar
to the statewide ban that started on January 1, 2021.
●  Further movement be put on hold until the National Academy of Science (NAS) completes their
review of scientific literature of sunscreen's impact on both environmental and human health.
The NAS should publish a report in spring 2022 and will give decision makers guidance on how to
approach sunscreen rulings.
Following are advisories/ recommendations by the FDA and DOH when considering Bill 135:
●  The FDA recommended no changes to currently marketed sunscreens. The FDA is studying
chemical UV filters in sunscreens, but does not recommend banning them for use.
●  In a correspondence from the Hawaii DOH dated August 2, 2021: from a skin cancer/ human
health perspective, it is NOT advisable to limit sunscreens to only zinc/ titanium.
While working for many years in Waikiki, there is an observable need for sun care products of all types,
such as those found in some make-up and cosmetic products. Satisfying the needs and protecting the
health of individuals requires consideration when reviewing Bill 135.
We would like to continue servicing our guests both locally and from abroad by providing them with
choices in needed sun protection during their stay in Hawaii. As we who live here know, activities
requiring sunscreen protection are not only for swimming, but also for other outdoor activities such as
running, hiking, golfing, yardwork... Let's help minimize potential sun related health hazards for our
people and guests of Hawaii due to limited choice and limited availability.
Thank you for allowing me the opportunity to share this testimony.
Curtis Higashiyama
Employee Relations & Government Affairs Manager
ABC Stores

November 17, 2021
Dear Maui County Council
I am writing to you today to express my support for Bill 135. This bill is very important to me and a lot
of people. Throughout this school year, my classmates and I learned about the effects of non reef
safe sunscreen. Apparently the non reef safe sunscreen is dangerous to coral and humans. A lot of
non reef safe sunscreen says it is “reef safe” but it still contains oxybenzone and many other harmful
chemical ingredients. At this current rate of coral bleaching, soon there will be no more coral reefs. If
that happens the ecosystem will be in chaos. A lot of fish depend on coral reefs for food and
protection. A lot of marine species will go extinct. Seventy percent of coral reefs are damaged. Cora!
in Hawaii grow very slowly and are dying faster every year. To try to stop this, everyone needs this bill
to pass. If you know that coral reefs are dying at an extreme rate pass the bill. If this bill passes, this
could be the start to completely banning non reef safe sunscreen around the globe. According to
studies (at the current rate of bleaching) they estimate that in 2050, ninety percent of coral reefs will
go extinct! If all the coral reefs go extinct, twenty five percent of all marine life will also go extinct
because they rely on coral reefs. That is over one million marine species extinct and a billion would
suffer from humans using the wrong sunscreen! Also millions of people would lose their food source
with the lack of fish. If there are no reefs there would be no fish to fish and the economy would “take a
major hit”. The people who fish for a living would lose their jobs and would also starve because they
probably have fish as their main diet. Fish is the number one consumed meat in the world by fifty two
tons (over chicken). That would cause people to starve from hunger. Coral reefs also protect/shield
coastlines from storms and erosion. Around fourteen thousand tons of sunscreen go into the ocean
every year and a lot of it is deadly to coral reefs. Wrapping this all together, using reef safe sunscreen
instead of non reef safe sunscreen is no doubt beneficial to marine life and to humans. Please pass
this bill for everyone.
Sincerely
Mason Hu

Bill 135
To:
Subject:

)ear Maui Council
I am writing to you today to express my support for Bill 135
Bill 135 states the movement of banning Non-reef safe sunscreen. Section 1 of this bill states that even though
the 2 main sunscreen ingredients were banned (oxybenzone and octinoxate) these are not the only chemicals
that are harmful to the coral reefs. The bill states that the Maui Council has marked the 2 safe chemicals in
sunscreen (zinc oxide and titanium dioxide) as Generally Recognized as safe AndEffective (GRASE). GfRASE
shows that the ingredients are safe and effective. Although these ingredients have been marked as GRASE,
the Council has not yet accepted the other 12 chemicals to be GRASE. These chemicals are avobenzone,
cinoxate, dioxybenzone, ensulizole, homosalate, meradimate, octinoxate, octisalate, octocrylene, oxybenzone,
padimate O, and sulisobenzone. These ingredients are marked by companies and stores as “reef friendly” but
not exactly “reef safe.” These are the chemicals that are still impacting coral reefs. This Bill 135 is trying to ban
these substances as they are still not safe for coral reefs or any other living organisms.
Sincerely
Jacob James
Kihei Charter School 7th Grade

County Council Meeting 11/19 - Strong Support for 'Aina Kupuna, Bill 118
To:
Subject:
You don't often get email from kkawaiaea@gmail.com. Learn why this is important
H na hanohano o ka 'Aha Kalana o Maui, Chair Lee, Vice-Chair Rawlins-Fernadez and members of the Maui
Council,
Aloha nui ‘oukou;
My name is Keiki Chang Kawai'ae'a and I am writing to express my STRONG SUPPORT for the ‘aina kupuna
tax dedication Bill 118. ‘Aina kupuna, are ancestral lands, a home or place that has been lived on and
cherished for generations. It includes land in all forms and types, residential lots, agricultural and pastoral
lands, beach and forests that can be traced back through genealogical ownership three or more generations.
Those who claim ‘aina kupuna can demonstrate visible or physical symbols of family continuity, use and or
relationship with the land.
‘Ohana with ancestral lands have deep rooted connections, aloha to place and have made important
contributions to community through their genealogical, cultural, scientific, and historical ties to and with the
land. For many ‘ohana like ours, it has been an overwhelming challenge to hold on to ‘aina kupuna, especially
due to the developing upscale high end speculation homes and development in Makena where our ‘aina
kupuna are located.
Councilmember Rawlins-Fernandez has created a bill that addresses this long-standing problem. It is a
landmark bill, that you the County Council have pulled together to support in its first reading. I am grateful, as is
my family, for the hope that you have given us through support of Bill 118. I humbly ask for your continued
support in the passing of Bill 118 in its final second reading.

Testimony for 'Aina Kupuna initiative Bill 118
To:
ICE OF THE
COUNTY CLERK
oSubject:
You don't often get email from danamalina@yahoo.com. Learn why this is important
, Dana Keawe, support Bill 118 and I humbly ask to pass Bill 118 into law for the following important
reasons:
Native Hawaiian and kama'aina families who have been able to maintain their ancestral lands for
generations represent a foundation of Maui's historical and cultural legacy, and help to maintain
important connections to the past and to the ‘aina that have informed, and continue to inform, Maui's
social fabric and unique community values. This bill will help more of these families hold on to their
'ohana lands, especially amidst global real estate speculation, skyrocketing property values, and
resulting property tax assessments that may exceed what many can afford. Accordingly, this
measure will help to perpetuate Maui's historical and cultural legacy, and preserve that which has
helped to make Maui and all of Hawai'i such a unique and special place to live.
Land grabs and speculation by off-island investors should never lead to long-time kama'aina families
being taxed into poverty, or off of their ancestral lands. This bill will protect Maui's families and the
legacy they represent, from property tax increases due to forces well beyond their control.
The dispossession of land has deep, profound, and unique impacts on Native Hawaiians, whose
health and well-being are based on their feelings for and deep attachment to the ‘aina. Other
kama'aina who have maintained their family lands for generations are likely to have also developed a
deep, familial attachment to their lands that would be devastating to lose. This bill will provide critical
protection for Native Hawaiian and other ‘ohana who may be forced to choose between the
devastation of selling their ancestral lands, or paying tax assessments that they are increasingly
unable to afford.
The county government has benefited greatly from skyrocketing property values and associated
property taxes, driven by real estate speculation, foreign investment, and the global demand for land
in Hawai'i. Sadly, this surge in property values is now pushing Maui's long-time 'ohana to the brink of
losing their ancestral lands, going into poverty to pay their property taxes, or monetizing their ‘aina in
ways that erode their character, and the overall character of Maui's unique communities. As its
coffers continue to fill from the foreign desire for Maui's lands, the county must take steps to provide
targeted tax relief for its long-time 'ohana, and the last living vestiges of Maui's social and cultural
heritage that they embody.
Sincerely,
Dana Keawe

To: Maui County Council
Re: Bill No. 135 A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE ESTABLISHING CHAPTER 20.42, MAUI
PROHIBIT THE SALE, USE, OR DISTRIBUTION OF NON-MINERAL SUNSCREENS
Position: STRONG SUPPORT
Hearing Date: Friday, November 19, 2021, 9 a.m.
Aloha Honorable Alice L. Lee, Chair, Keani Rawlins-Fernandez Vice Chair, and Councilmembers
Coral reefs are intrinsic to Hawaiian culture and provide critical natural protection against coastal erosion and
sea level rise and are a viable food source for our communities. Further, our coral reefs underpin our tourism
industry, Hawai'i's vital economic engine. Currently, these reefs we depend on are at risk. Where people use
marine environments as recreational resources, there is sunscreen pollution. Swimmers put on sunscreen
products before they enter into the water and over a period of an hour much of that sunscreen will slough off,
potentially contaminating the surrounding water. This is a grave concern because it has been reported in the
scientific literature that non-mineral sunscreens can have irreversibly detrimental effects on marine life,
including changes in fish behavior, damage to coral DNA and larvae, and the health of algae, fish, shellfish,
urchins, and marine mammals.
The National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration has already recognized this existential threat to our
coral reefs (See: https://oceanservice.noaa.gov/news/sunscreen-corals.html)
SUNSCREEN CHEMICALS AND MARINE LIFE

On September 24, 2021, the FDA issued a proposed order concerning nonprescription sunscreen drug products.
In the proposed order, two mineral products zinc oxide and titanium dioxide are deemed generally recognized
as safe and effective (GRASE), and fourteen products are deemed NOT GRASE. Of the fourteen products,
twelve products do not currently contain sufficient data to support positive GRASE classification. The twelve
products that require additional data are avobenzone, cinoxate, dioxybenzone, ensulizole, homosalate,
meradimate, octinoxate, octisalate, octocrylene, oxybenzone, padimate 0, and sulisobenzone.

We ask your strong support for Bid 135 prohibiting the saie, use, or distribution of non-mineral sunscreens that
have questionable effects on the health of humans and marine life in alignment with the Precautionary
Principle which asserts that the burden of proof for potentiady harmful actions by industry or government
rests on the assurance of safety and that when there are threats of serious damage, scientific uncertainty
must be resolved In favor of prevention, affording us the opportunity to protect our environment and
communities for future generations.
